Measures for Clearing Land in the Disaster Area 163

Announced by the Municipal Land Bureau

Regarding the sale and transfer of land in the disaster area, the Municipal Land Bureau previously issued a notice to suspend transfers to prevent disputes arising from the displacement of people after the war. At the same time, it carefully planned measures to clear the land in the disaster area. This plan has now been submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and was officially announced yesterday. The original text reads as follows: "Notice is hereby given. According to Shanghai Municipal Government Order No. 970, after the recent war in Wusong, Jiangwan, Zhabei, Yinxiang, Yinhang, Pengpu, Zhenru, and other districts of this city, most of the local buildings were destroyed by artillery fire, and prosperous areas have become scorched earth. Most of the original boundaries have lost their original appearance. Even the various contracts and documents owned by various business owners were hastily abandoned during the incident and were either reduced to ashes or lost. At this time of preparation for reconstruction, it is extremely important to reorganize boundaries and protect property rights. Under these special circumstances, if theft and illegal buying and selling occur again, it will not only be difficult to investigate, but also easily lead to disputes. In addition to the reorganization of roads, which has been ordered to be handled by the Public Works Bureau in conjunction with this bureau, the relevant bureau is hereby ordered to immediately comply with the following: All land contracts, sales, and transfers in the above-mentioned war-affected areas should be temporarily suspended. At the same time, the bureau should actively prepare fundamental clearing measures. All reported households should be surveyed and registered in advance to prevent disputes. Please comply immediately and report the progress of the implementation within a specified time limit, etc." The bureau's petition and proposed clearing measures for the disaster-stricken areas and attachments have been discussed and approved at the temporary municipal meeting on May 24th, and the bureau's original proposed measures have been amended and passed. An official document is hereby issued to be copied and distributed for public knowledge. This order and attachments will be filed separately, and the amended measures are attached to the bureau for compliance. Upon receiving this order, the measures are hereby copied and announced to all business owners in the above-mentioned districts of this city for their full knowledge. This notice.

Attached: Measures for Clearing Land in the War Zone. (1) For all cases within Wusong, Jiangwan, Zhabei, Yinxiang, Yinhang, Pengpu, and Zhenru districts that have previously been cleared, surveyed, and re-certified, as well as cleared, surveyed, and supplemented with certificates, and cleared, surveyed, and established boundaries, they shall be processed first. (2) Many houses in Wusong, Jiangwan, and Zhabei have been destroyed. The boundaries of households and land shall be surveyed by personnel dispatched by this bureau, stationed in various locations, based on topographic maps and the evidence of neighboring property owners, to clarify the boundaries. (3) If property owners have lost land certificates or field deeds, or other proof of property rights due to unclear land boundaries after the war, they shall, within three months, find reliable shopkeepers to guarantee them and report to this bureau for registration, so that a public notice can be published and supplementary procedures can be expedited. (4) In all disaster-stricken areas, if the boundaries of households and land are still clear and the proof of property rights is completely intact, and a transfer is requested, the bureau shall publish a public notice. If no one raises an objection within two months, it shall be approved. June 4, 21st year of the Republic of China, Director Jin Liren.

The Social Bureau's Plan to Restore the Economy of the Poor in the War Zone 164

Expanding the Poor People's Loan Fund

Planning for Farmer Relief

After the devastation of the war in Zhabei, Jiangwan, Wusong, Zhenru and other places in this city, the houses have become ruins and the population is sparse, with desolation everywhere. Mr. Wu Xingya, Director of the Municipal Social Bureau, after taking office, immediately witnessed the devastation of Zhabei. He worked hard to provide relief. In addition to submitting various relief measures to the Municipal Government for review, he also sent Zhang Binghui, Chief of the Fourth Section, to attend the meeting of the Shanghai War Zone Relief Committee, reporting on the two most important measures in the bureau's proposed relief plan: one is to expand the Poor People's Loan Fund, and the other is to assist farmers in resuming their businesses. The Poor People's Loan Fund in this city suffered greatly from the direct impact of the war. Although the Nanshi Loan Fund has been restored to its original state, the borrowers in various war zones are scattered and almost non-existent. It is difficult to restore the old situation. However, for the sake of promoting local prosperity and assisting the poor in making a living, restoration cannot be delayed. The original fund of the Loan Fund was 40,200 yuan. After the January 28th Incident, most of the loans due in various districts could not be recovered. The remaining funds deposited in various banks were only over 15,000 yuan. Although it is not impossible to recover the uncollected funds, it is necessary to allow for a longer period of time in practice. After the resumption of business, there will inevitably be more borrowers. The deposit of over 10,000 yuan may not be enough to meet the distribution of requests within a week, even if only considering Zhabei. It is estimated that there are 3,000 borrowing households, and each household needs 20 yuan according to regulations, which requires 60,000 yuan. For the helpless poor who have difficulty finding shopkeepers to guarantee them, it is proposed to set up a separate emergency interest-free loan with a term of one year. If each household is loaned 5 yuan, and there are 5,000 households, another 25,000 yuan is needed. The situation in Wusong and Jiangwan is the same, and it is estimated that 5,000 yuan will be allocated to each district, which requires 10,000 yuan. As for agricultural loans in Zhenru, Pengpu, and other rural areas, efforts should be made to expand them. At 1,000 yuan per district, another 10,000 yuan is needed. In total, the recovery and expansion of the Loan Fund's business requires a fund of more than 100,000 yuan. Although the municipal treasury is stretched and it is difficult to raise a large sum of money, this relief effort is based on the recovery of principal and is of great benefit to the economy of the common people. It should be prioritized. As for the rural economy, the war damage suffered is difficult to estimate. It is proposed to start with an investigation and then provide relief separately. The measures are: (1) Allocate funds to subsidize farmers to purchase seeds, fertilizers, plows, and farming tools. (2) Reduce or exempt new and old land taxes. All the committee members believe that the above plan is an urgent task and should be listed as a proposal. It was unanimously decided to hand it over to the Relief Group for review and submit it for discussion at the next meeting.

Shanghai Banks Jointly Establish China Credit Reporting Agency 166

The First Cry of Chinese Nationals Running Their Own Credit Reporting Agency

Officially Established Tomorrow on Yuanmingyuan Road

The purpose of establishing a credit reporting agency is to investigate industrial and commercial credit, disseminate market information, and serve as a compass for the financial sector, so as to avoid investment difficulties, realize economic cooperation, and promote social prosperity. All European and American countries attach importance to it. Shanghai is an international commercial hub. In the past, regarding credit reporting facts, in addition to the Japanese-run Tokyo Credit Bureau, Imperial Credit Bureau, and Shanghai Credit Bureau, etc., the two American-owned companies mainly focused on compiling directories. Only the banks run by Chinese nationals have investigation departments, and independent organizations are still lacking. After the Shanghai war, the industry and commerce that were ravaged and devastated eagerly looked forward to the assistance of the financial sector, and the establishment of a credit reporting agency came into being. The China Credit Reporting Agency was initiated and organized by banks such as the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications. The address is at No. 1 Yuanmingyuan Road, and it is scheduled to be officially established on the morning of the 6th of this month. The details are described below:

Initiating Motivation: In addition to establishing their own investigation departments, major banks such as the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications in this port also have the organization of the China Credit Association. This China Credit Association is only a mechanism for banks to communicate with each other. The qualifications for joining the association are quite strict, and it does not have any external relations. After the outbreak of the Shanghai war, industries and businesses in decline were increasingly eager for assistance from the financial sector, and the financial sector itself felt more and more difficult to invest. Therefore, the organization of the China Credit Reporting Agency was initiated to openly specialize in credit reporting facts. Members of the China Credit Association are its basic members.

Participating Banks: The banks that have joined the China Credit Reporting Agency include the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the Central Bank, the China Industrial Bank, the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank, the Guohua Bank, the Zhongfu Bank, the Xinhua Bank, the Minghua Bank, the China Agricultural & Industrial Bank, and the Central Trust Company. It is reported that the Jin Cheng, Yanyeh, Zhongnan, and Continental banks will soon join.

Cholera is Unrelated to Huangpu River Water 171

Recently, some newspapers reported that the cholera in this port is related to the garbage piled up along the Huangpu River. According to the head of the Public Health Department of the Public Works Bureau, Shanghai has had a mortality rate of 1.2 out of 10,000 due to cholera in the past ten years, while Calcutta has had a rate of 10 to 20 out of 10,000. The problem of garbage accumulation should be seriously considered, but it cannot be said to be related to this disease. Cholera bacteria do not originate in garbage, and Shanghai has never had this disease in winter. The reason is probably that many small boats bring the disease from areas with cholera and contaminate the water of the Huangpu River. For example, the discovery of cholera in Hankou is usually earlier than in Shanghai, which seems to be evidence. It is difficult to say for sure whether the early discovery this year is due to the early occurrence of the disease elsewhere, but it is likely to be the case. As for the garbage problem, there is no need to mention them together, so there is no need to worry.

The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association Calls for Strict Enforcement of the Opium Ban 172

Submitting Opinions to the Central Political Council

The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association believes that the Central Government has recently strictly ordered the abolition of the opium special tax in northern Anhui, and the Central Political Conference is also scheduled to discuss measures to strictly enforce the opium ban. On the one hand, there is a sign of starting anew with the people, but on the other hand, Liu Ruiheng, Chairman of the Anti-Smoking Committee, has petitioned the Executive Yuan, strongly arguing that the complete ban is not feasible, advocating a gradual ban policy, and continuing to collect opium taxes to fund the anti-smoking funds. The content is actually a disguised public sale method, which not only violates the Premier's anti-drug instructions, but also contradicts the principle of strict opium prohibition. It is deeply feared that once implemented, it will lead to endless disasters. Yesterday, in accordance with the resolution of the General Assembly, a letter was sent to the Central Political Conference to convey the people's demands. The original letter is recorded below: "Respectfully, the survival of the opium ban concerns the future of the Party and the country, and the fate of the nation. In the past, the Central Government did not have a clear position on the opium ban, which led to widespread rumors and criticisms. Recently, various provinces have competed to publicly sell opium, and there are also rumors that the Central Government is also preparing to implement it. The Association received this bad news with panic and horror, so telegrams were sent to express opposition, sincerely hoping to promote the authorities' awareness with good medicine. However, we hope that these rumors will not become a reality. In recent days, the Central Government has issued several strict orders regarding the strict enforcement of the opium ban. The corrupt officials who handled the special tax on opium seedlings in Anhui Province have been dismissed and arrested. The Executive Yuan has also issued an order to the Anti-Smoking Committee to send commissioners to various provinces to investigate the public sale of opium. The news has spread far and wide, and people are cheering and applauding. Also, reading today's newspaper, the Committee is scheduled to meet on the 4th to review the anti-smoking measures, and all the commissioners advocated a thorough ban, etc. It is hoped that from now on, China's anti-smoking policy will have a day of clarity. However, there is still something to ask of the Committee: The special tax in Hunan and Hubei has not been abolished, and the local authorities and the army stationed in Fujian are forcing the planting of opium, rampant as before. Zhang Xueliang's provinces of Jicharehsui under his jurisdiction are selling publicly. It is heard that someone is strongly promoting the special tax in Jiangsu Province. And the Chairman of the Anti-Smoking Committee, Liu Ruiheng, recently submitted his opinions on opium prohibition to the Executive Yuan, still strongly criticizing the infeasibility of the complete ban, advocating a gradual ban. To sum up the reasons put forward by Liu, it is nothing more than the complete ban offending the powerful and having no profit to be made, and the gradual ban being able to rely on the collection of money from the opium ban as a source of finance, and prolonging the disaster of opium, combining the ban with the collection, and leaving the organizers of the opium ban with room for corruption and money-making. The specific measures are nothing more than a disguised public sale of opium. Therefore, Liu's so-called registration method and the administrative method of collecting money from the opium ban are all steps in the public sale of opium. This is Liu's unrepentant expression of evil, and will eventually be sworn against by the people to the death. We dare to implore the public to give full consideration to the above items, to uphold the Premier's anti-drug instructions, to base themselves on the people's anti-smoking demands, to uphold the spirit of thorough rule of law, to eliminate the great harm to the future of the Party and the country, to vote unanimously, and to hand them over to the Executive Yuan to clearly order the abolition of the special tax offices in Hunan and Hubei, and to order Zhang Xueliang to immediately abolish the public sale of opium, and to order the 19th Route Army, which is about to enter Fujian, to eradicate the opium seedlings in Fujian Province, to strictly enforce the opium ban, and to punish the illegal officials who have indulged the opium disaster in Fujian. To strictly crack down on the brewing of special taxes in Jiangsu, so that it will not be realized. To severely refute Liu Ruiheng's absurd proposal, and to punish him according to law based on the impeachment of the Supervisory Yuan, and to decide to adopt a policy of complete eradication, in order to comply with public opinion and establish a new model. The above points may already be under consideration and processing by the public, but the Association does not hesitate to speak in detail, but only to urge the public's attention. The way to plan for the country is no greater than promoting benefits and eliminating harms. Opium is a great harm to the country, and its disaster has been going on for nearly a hundred years. If it can be eliminated in the public's administration, it will be a great achievement and virtue that will shine through the ages. We dare to express our humble opinions and humbly ask you to adopt and implement them with the utmost sincerity. This letter is addressed to the Central Political Conference Committee."

Local News Two

Zhang Xi Suggests Building a Sea Gate on the Sheyang River 175

Zhang Xi, representative of the Fu Ge Salt Land Reclamation Company, submitted a document to the National Government Relief for Flood Victims Committee, stating that the representatives of various salt land reclamation companies in the Lixiahe region of Jiangsu province respectfully request equal treatment in order to fully complete the work on the five rivers and establish water conservancy for generations to come.

The five ports of Lixiahe, which connect to the sea, are essential channels for draining accumulated water from the entire Jiangbei region, and particularly important for diverting floodwaters from the Huai River. However, due to the winding river channels, water cannot be discharged smoothly annually. Whenever the Grand Canal is breached, the five counties of Lixiahe are flooded, causing disaster. In years of drought, freshwater is completely drained, and saltwater encroaches on the inland, making it difficult to find even a drop of freshwater in Dongtai, Yancheng, and Funing. Not only is there no water for irrigation, but drinking water is also cut off, even leading to the breeding of locusts (tiny fish and shrimp are carried ashore by saltwater tides, and when the tide recedes, the fish and shrimp are left to bake in the sun, becoming "jumping locusts"), afflicting both the north and south banks of the Yangtze River. The disasters of past years are well-known to the world, and the scale of the suffering is unparalleled.

After last year's major flood, the government understood the root cause and planned to dredge and straighten the five ports of Lixiahe and build saltwater barriers at Wanggang, Zhugang, and Doulonggang. However, because the Sheyang River basin is too large, there were no resources to build a gate, so it was not dredged or straightened. Consequently, the 15th District Work Relief Bureau was not established. The representatives understand the difficulties of the National Government in allocating relief funds and the unavoidable delay, but the construction of a gate and the dredging and straightening of the Sheyang River are more important than the several ports of Wanggang, Zhugang, and Doulonggang, affecting the interests of the entire Jiangbei region.

It is crucial to remember that while disasters in the Yangtze River basin occur only every few decades, Jiangbei suffers from either floods or droughts almost every year. The National Government spent tens of millions of dollars to repair the main dikes of the Yangtze River, while completing the work in Jiangbei would cost only a few million dollars. Moreover, Jiangsu is a model province, and Jiangbei is the capital's shield. How can we allow it to suffer from disasters year after year, forcing tens of millions of people, impoverished and starving, to become bandits?

Therefore, the representatives dare to present this request to your esteemed committee, hoping that you will consider the above facts, vigorously raise relief funds, and construct a sea gate on the Sheyang River, as well as straighten the river channel, so that water can be discharged smoothly in wet years and freshwater can be retained for disaster relief in dry years. Then, Jiangbei, known as a barren and bandit-ridden area, will be transformed into a fertile and cultured region. This achievement will last for generations.

For many years, we have been deeply concerned and have appealed without success. Now, fortunately, as your esteemed committee is implementing good policies to improve the waterways of Lixiahe, we sincerely petition you to consider and adopt our proposal to complete the work.

Furthermore, it should be noted that each salt land reclamation company has built its own sea dikes and gates and opened its own river channels. Their local land reclamation work is self-funded and does not rely on the use of the five ports or river gates. The above request is made because we have been engaged in land reclamation in Jiangbei for many years and have more experience and clear observations. It is made for the sake of the people and public security, not for the benefit of the companies. This is supported by facts that can be verified.

This petition is submitted to the National Government Relief for Flood Victims Committee by Zhang Xi, representative of the Yancheng and Funing Salt Land Reclamation Companies, June 3rd, Year 21.

Businesses in the War Zone (Water, Electricity, Shops, Automobile Dealers, etc.) 177

Lost Licenses: Free Replacement

Business Closure: Exemption from License Renewal

The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities issued a notice yesterday stating that after the January 28th Incident, licenses originally obtained by water pipe suppliers, electrical material stores, automobile dealers, and gas stations within the war zone may have been damaged or lost. Replacements should be applied for according to regulations. However, in consideration of the circumstances, those whose licenses have been destroyed will be granted free replacements, but they must also pay for a frame to ensure uniformity. Businesses whose licenses have been destroyed and have declared that they have ceased operations will be allowed to cancel their licenses and will be exempt from applying for new licenses.

All relevant stores and firms should promptly report the facts to the bureau for processing.

Both Roads Bureau and Various Offices Moved Yesterday 184

Since the January 28th Incident, the Two Roads Bureau and its subordinate offices have been operating from No. 6 and No. 10 Sichuan Road, Guizhou Road, Yuanmingyuan Road, and other locations for four months. Shanghai Ferry Launches Songhu Special Service 185

Facilitating Visits to the War Zone

The municipal ferry has launched the Songhu special service to maintain transportation between Shanghai and Wusong. It departs from the Bund bronze statue pier on Nanjing Road at 7:30 AM, 10:30 AM, and 1:30 PM daily, heading directly to Songzhen. It returns from Wusong at 9:00 AM, 12:00 PM, and 3:30 PM, without stopping at any ports along the way. The journey takes only one hour. From the town, it is only about a mile's walk to Fort Baotai, which is extremely convenient. Recently, various war zones have been taken over one after another, and people from this city have been flocking to visit and pay their respects. However, transportation to the Wusong area has been inconvenient, and vehicles have not been able to reach it directly, which is regrettable. Even the Shanghai-Songhu train only goes as far as Yunzaobang. Therefore, the municipal ferry special service is the most convenient way to visit the Wusong area.

Renovation and Opening of the South Shanghai Wharf 186

Authorities Strictly Prohibit Gangsters from Extorting Money

The public wharves in this city have been placed under the management of the Municipal Government's Public Utilities Bureau, which has designated the Wharf and Warehouse Management Office to oversee them. Recently, the renovation of the South Shanghai Wharf by the Public Works Bureau has been completed, and it has been officially opened as a public wharf. Ships are not charged for berthing. However, local gangsters used to take advantage of merchants and boatmen loading and unloading goods at the wharf by extorting money. The bureau, in conjunction with the Public Security Bureau, has notified all merchants and boatmen that if they encounter the above situation, they should immediately report it to the Wharf Police Station in District 1 of the Public Security Bureau or the Wharf and Warehouse Management Office of the Public Utilities Bureau for investigation and punishment.

Notice for Those Applying for Certificates of National Products 187

The Shanghai National Products Exhibition Hall, due to the intense patriotic movement, was concerned that domestic goods might be mistakenly seized. It specially obtained approval from higher authorities to issue certificates of national products for identification. However, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce also issued such certificates at that time. To facilitate matters for all manufacturers and to seek uniformity, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has stopped issuing them. Its 93rd Standing Committee meeting resolved to notify all manufacturers with previously issued certificates to apply for replacements from the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs National Products Exhibition Hall before June 20th, in accordance with the law. After June 20th, the association will publish an announcement stating that previously issued certificates will no longer be valid. The address of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs National Products Exhibition Hall has now been moved to the fourth floor of the Sugar, Dried Goods, and Sundries Trade Association Building at Xiaodongmen in the South City. Normal operations are being carried out. It is also reported that Zheng Qi, the director of the hall, has resigned and his resignation has been approved. Yu Tianbi, a staff member of the second section of the bureau, has been appointed as acting director.

The National Products Market at the intersection of Dasheng Street and Xiaodongmen, and the China National Rubber Products United Distribution Office, are nearing completion day and night and are scheduled to open on June 7th. It is expected that there will be a grand occasion at that time.

Ratepayers Association Sends Letter to Shanghai Municipal Council Requesting Punishment of Western Constable for Assaulting Vendor 190

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association sent a letter to the Secretary of the Shanghai Municipal Council yesterday regarding the assault of a vendor by a Western constable from the Xinzha Police Station.

The letter reads:

Respected Sir,

According to Wang Tingliang's statement to the association, he makes a living as a vendor and conducts his business peacefully. On the morning of May 29th, at 8:30 AM, he was selling undershirts in Tongheli, Maigen Road, in the Public Concession. Suddenly, Western Constable No. 64 from the Xinzha Road Police Station rushed over, threatening to beat him. To avoid his violent aggression, the vendor fled into a house. The constable chased after him, and without asking the reason, relied on his strength to beat him repeatedly. He was then taken to the police station and beaten with a rattan cane, causing serious injuries to his shoulders, arms, waist, and back. Although he was released at the time, he had difficulty moving.

Considering that in this chaotic world, firewood is as expensive as cassia and rice is as precious as pearls, his family of three, including his elderly mother and younger brother, all rely on him for their livelihood. It is not easy for poor people to make a living, and those who do not become beggars are few and far between. Yet, even this small business has been frustrated. The vendor reported this to the Gordon Road Police Station, which sent a Western constable to the Xinzha Road Police Station to inquire. He was then sent to Renji Hospital for treatment and medication, and a report of injury was issued. The Chinese constable sent by the police station brought him back to the police station. The vendor is still suffering from pain from his injuries and cannot work.

Therefore, we again request that your association, based on the principles of law and humanity, forward this letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council for handling. We would be most grateful.

He also showed his injuries. The vendor was originally taking a risk to make a living, and the vendor was doing business in the neighborhood, which did not seem to hinder traffic. The Western constable's interference was beyond the scope of his authority, and his arbitrary beating of the vendor caused injury. The exercise of his powers was excessive. Furthermore, we have heard that fines are not processed for less than one yuan, which is close to being harsh and will only force vendors to become beggars and robbers.

Therefore, we urge your bureau to be lenient and provide relief to the general vendors. We also urge you to provide medical treatment and compensation to the victim and punish the Western constable in accordance with the law.

Emergency Meeting of the Tenants Association 191

The Shanghai Special Municipality Tenants Association convened an emergency meeting of representatives from various Lane Associations yesterday at 2:00 PM. More than one hundred people attended. Cheng Kefan was elected chairman. The chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting and discussed the following items:

(1) The case of petitioning the Municipal Government to revise the submission. (Resolution) Revised and passed.

(2) Measures to reduce or exempt rent separately. Please ask the authorities to announce them promptly to avoid prolonging disputes. (Resolution) Formulate specific measures separately and submit them to the Municipal Government for review and approval so that they can be followed.

(3) The case of the Association unifying and strengthening its organization. (Resolution) Each branch association should register with the Association immediately to facilitate investigation.

(4) The case of the Association's election in the 21st year. (Resolution) An election meeting will be convened once the registration procedures are completed.

(5) The Hengli Lane representative reported that the landlords had automatically reduced rent for three months in various places. (Resolution) Thank you.

(6) The case of the second landlord and the second tenant demanding a rent reduction or exemption. (Resolution) The second landlord and the third tenant should be treated equally. Electricity bills, etc., should be provided as usual. Those who rented after the war should not enjoy the above rights.

(7) The case of nominating five petition representatives. (Resolution) Chen Jiufeng, Zhou Xinyou, Cheng Kefan, Pan Zhenshu, and Shan Xingwu were nominated and will depart on Monday morning.

(8) Should the rent reduction be stipulated? (Resolution) It shall be handled at the discretion of the Municipal Government, taking into account the circumstances.

(9) Provisional motion case. (Resolution) Omitted.

(10) The meeting adjourned at 7:00 PM.

Clever Design of an Opium Den 192

Thick Hemp Rope Suspended Outside the Back Window

Ensuring Opium Smokers Can Escape

Jiang Xiansheng, also known as Jia Xiansheng, a native of Hangzhou, is currently 41 years old. He previously rented a three-story building at No. 2 Xiangyuanli, Xiaodongmen Street, in the French Concession. The building was located on the border between the Chinese and French concessions, with the back door facing Dongmen Road in the Chinese area. Jiang divided the house into dozens of rooms of varying sizes and sublet them to others, who opened opium dens. The rent for each room ranged from 20 to 35 yuan per month. He enjoyed a huge profit as a second landlord and had accumulated a considerable fortune.

In February of this year, the French police discovered this and arrested the owner of the opium den, his accomplices, smokers, and Jiang together, and sent them to court for interrogation. In addition to sentencing those who had set up the dens privately, Jiang was acquitted and released due to insufficient evidence. However, Jiang did not repent and continued his business as a second landlord, subletting the house as usual and opening an opium den. He even went a step further and collected insurance fees from the tenants. He also hung a thick hemp rope outside the back windows of the second and third floors so that if the police detectives came to arrest them, the smokers and the den staff could be notified to escape through the windows and down the rope into the Chinese area. His ingenious design was very clever.

However, the plan was discovered by the French police, and on the afternoon of the 2nd, at 9:00 PM, Head Detectives Mao Jingen and Mao Jinsheng, Deputy Detectives Wang Rusong and Jiang Changwen, along with Bao Tangu Mingzhou, Lu Jinxiang, and others, went to the house along with the Western detectives. They first arrested Jiang and then searched the rooms. By this time, the owners and customers of the opium dens in the rooms on the second floor had already heard the news and escaped down the rope. Only two families were found on the third floor.

In room No. 8, they found Ma Agen, a native of Suzhou who had set up the den privately, his assistant Wang Yuanfu, and smokers Lu Genshou, Zhou Shaotang, and Zhu Baosheng. In room No. 12, they found Dai Wu'bao, a native of Changshu who had set up the den privately, his assistant Zhang Youquan, and customers Xue Bingnan and Fan Kunyu. A large number of opium paraphernalia and lamps were confiscated, and 12 bags of opium paste were found on Wang Yuanfu's body. Opium lamps were also found in the rooms of women Li Mao's and Zhang Asheng, but no one was smoking opium inside.

Jiang and the 12 men and women were all taken to the police station. The next day, they were sent to the Second Special Court for investigation. The police charged Mao Li's and Zhang Asheng with illegally possessing opium paraphernalia under Article 13 of the Anti-Opium Law. In the morning, Judge Zhang Chaozu presided over a preliminary hearing in the Second Criminal Court. The defendants admitted to illegally possessing opium paraphernalia. Zhang Asheng was defended by Jin Yu, a lawyer. Li was sentenced to a fine of 300 yuan, and Zhang was fined 80 yuan. If they were unable to pay, they would be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan.

The police charged Jiang and the other ten people with violations of Articles 10 and 11 of the Anti-Opium Law. In the afternoon, Judge Wang Gangxu presided over a hearing in the First Criminal Court. First, the police lawyer Fei Xizhen stated the facts of the case and presented the opium paraphernalia and hemp rope as evidence. Bao Tan Gu Mingzhou then reported on the process of cracking the defendants' case.

When questioned, Jiang denied that he was still subletting the house to others to open opium dens. He claimed that after being arrested and released last time, he returned the lease to the big landlord and only rented one room for himself to live in. He had published a statement in the newspaper at the end of March. He was defended by Jin Yu and lawyer Liu Shiqi.

Ma Agen, Dai Wu'bao, Wang Yuanfu, Zhang Youquan, and others confessed that they had rented the house from Jiang to set up opium dens privately. The smokers, including Chen Shougen, confessed to smoking opium. The court verified the confessions and ordered further verification. The defendants were returned to the police station.

Intimidating Robbers by Threatening Kidnapping 193

He Yongli Alone in the Room

The Victim Called the Police to Arrest Him

Chen Yushun, the owner of Hengtai Seafood Store on Rue de l'Amiral Bayle (洋行街) in the French Concession, suddenly received a threatening letter on May 31st, demanding 10,000 yuan. The letter stipulated that the money be sent to the Nanyang Hotel at Xiaodongmen (小東門) on Min'guo Road (民國路) on the afternoon of June 3rd, otherwise, they would resort to kidnapping. Chen then sent Xu and his cousin, Jiang Lianfu, to go as agreed. Upon arrival, they met He Yongli, a Ningbo native. According to He, the meeting place had been changed to the Nanyang Hotel on North Zhejiang Road (北浙江路), and the time was still 9:30 AM. After saying this, they parted ways. When Jiang Lianfu went alone to room number three of the Nanyang Hotel on North Zhejiang Road as scheduled, he only saw He sitting idly in the room. After talking briefly, Jiang felt that this petty thief was not worth fearing, so he turned and ran out, calling for the police to enter and arrest He at the Concession police station. After questioning by the police chief, it was learned that He's home was upstairs in the Tongbao Tai Hotel dormitory at No. 624 Xipuyi Lane (西普益里), Qipu Road (七浦路). Detectives Shang Wu were dispatched overnight to search He's home, where they only found his concubine in the room. Afterwards, they went to a certain place to arrest accomplices, but they had already escaped in advance. Yesterday morning, He was escorted to the First Special District Court, where Judge Shen Bingrong interrogated him. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang requested that the suspect be temporarily detained because the case was still under investigation, and that a formal prosecution would be filed after the investigation was completed. Judge Shen then asked Jiang Lianfu about the negotiation process and approved a postponement to wait for the investigation to be completed before further questioning. He Yongli was still taken back to the Concession police station for detention.

Traveler Commits Suicide by Poison 194

On the morning of the 3rd, at 11:30 AM, a traveler came to the Jiangsu Hotel at No. 202 Guangdong Road (廣東路). He called himself Zhou Chunshan, 22 years old, and came to Shanghai from Suzhou. He checked into room 106. Around 3:00 AM yesterday, he suddenly committed suicide by swallowing poison in his room. A tea server noticed this and reported it to the police station, who sent him to the Jiyuan Hospital (濟醫院) for treatment. Unfortunately, he had taken too much poison and died upon arrival at the hospital. Therefore, the reason for the suicide could not be ascertained. The body was sent to the coroner's office to await a court autopsy.

Police Officer's Wife Dies by Suicide by Poison 195

Unemployment and Economic Hardship Due to the Shanghai War

A Quarrel Between Husband and Wife Leads to a Drastic Change

The woman, Sun Li, was 26 years old. Her husband, Sun Anbang, was a police officer at the Fourth Division of the Fifth District at No. 7 Mayushan Road (馬玉山路). Since the Shanghai War, the area had been directly affected. As a result, Sun also suffered significant losses. Although the situation is gradually recovering, Sun's financial situation is extremely difficult. On the 2nd of this month, the couple had a quarrel over this. Feeling extremely remorseful, Mrs. Sun had a pessimistic thought. That night, she secretly took opium and committed suicide. When her husband noticed, her face was already pale. He immediately took her to Guangren Hospital (廣仁醫院), but the treatment was ineffective, and she died shortly after. The hospital reported to the Xinzha Police Station (新閘捕房), which ordered detectives to investigate. The body was taken to the forensic examination office on Faelen Road (斐倫路). Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court was requested to send Prosecutor Guo, along with forensic doctor Wei Ligong and clerk Wang Zuyi, to the office to examine the body. Prosecutor Guo took his seat and questioned Sun Anbang, who testified that he was from Shandong, 33 years old, and a police officer. The deceased was his wife. Recently, due to financial difficulties, she and I had a slight quarrel the day before, and she committed suicide. I did not hit her, etc. After receiving the testimony, Guo ruled that the deceased, Sun Li, had indeed died from poisoning herself. The body was handed over to her husband, Sun Anbang, who signed a bond to take it back for burial.

Two Business Groups Plan to Establish Clinics 200

Yao Juren, Wu Youqian, Cai Xunchen, Ren Nongxuan, and other standing committee members of the 35th District Branch of the Citizens' Union Association (市民聯合會) at No. 4 Xishui Fang (西渭水坊), Zhejiang Road (浙江路), Ningbo Road (寧波路), and the Joint Association of Business Circles of Ningbo, Tianjin, Guizhou, Guangxi, and Laohe Roads (勞合五路), considering that it is the summer season, the weather is getting hotter, and epidemics are rampant, and that there will inevitably be a major epidemic after the Shanghai Incident on January 28, have planned to establish clinics at the association, divided into Chinese and Western medicine departments. Publication of the Lost Notes of Liu Dabai, Former Deputy Minister of Education 204

During the war in Shanghai, our country lost a famous scholar, and those who knew him at home and abroad were deeply saddened. This is Liu Dabai, the former Deputy Minister of Education, who passed away in West Lake. Liu was honest and upright throughout his life, and his funeral expenses were collected by his friends on the lake. However, his works, such as the lingering and sorrowful poems, and many original insights on Chinese philology, are immortal. Recently, his friend Xu Weinan in Shanghai collected his handwritten notes and published a book called "Letters from Baiwu," with a total of eighty letters. Among them, Liu himself describes his thoughts, life, and condition in a detailed and touching way. Those who admire Liu should not fail to read it. Moreover, Liu's writing style is extremely beautiful, and the book is very suitable as a model for vernacular letters. The book is sold by Shanghai and provincial World Book Stores (世界書局), and the price is only three corners. The proceeds from the sale of the book will be donated to Liu's surviving family members.

Undutiful Son's Sentence About to Expire, Old Father Asks to Sever Ties 208

Son Kowtows in Court, Begging for Forgiveness

Old Father Leaves Angrily, Ignoring Him

Chen Fuchang, a Ningbo native, used to run a coal and grain business in Dongjiadu (董家渡), Pudong, and his life was quite good. Chen had two sons, both of whom were married. The eldest son had the style of his father, being diligent and thrifty. However, the second son, A Mao, did not think about learning and willingly entered the lower class, associating with common hooligans. Moreover, he was addicted to opium and often asked his father for money to squander. If he was not satisfied, he dared to be violent to his father. Chen Fuchang, seeing that his rebellious son repeatedly refused to repent and dared to declare that he would sell his wife and children, once reported his son, A Mao, to the Procuratorate of the District Court for violence against a senior relative and opium use. Later, the Criminal Court sentenced him to three months in prison and a fine of twenty yuan, and he was sent to Caohejing Prison for execution. Now that Chen Fuchang's son, A Mao, is about to be released, and he fears that he will relapse and suffer, he has hired lawyer Chao Kun to file a petition with the District Court, requesting to sever family ties in order to avoid future troubles. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhu Chengzan opened the trial and ordered Chen A Mao to be brought to court. Chen Fuchang testified, "I am 75 years old, a Ningbo native. He (referring to A Mao) asks for money to smoke every day, associates with gangsters. In the past four years, he has forcibly asked for money and even hit me. Such a rebellious son is rare in the world. I request to sever the father-son relationship." Chen A Mao testified, "I am 25 years old. I used to work in a coal yard, but now I am unemployed. I married at the age of seventeen and have a son. It is true that I smoke opium. I am now willing to repent." After testifying, he repeatedly kowtowed to his father in court, saying "Father, I know I was wrong. I will correct my mistakes in the future." He spoke and wept. Chen Fuchang turned his head and ignored him. The official said, "There are only unfilial sons in the world, and there are no parents who are not good. If you can really repent, then ask your relatives and friends to plead with your father for forgiveness." At this point in the interrogation, lawyer Chao Kun made a statement. The judge said, "This case is now considered concluded and will be pronounced on the eighth." After the ruling, the court adjourned, and the defendant, Chen A Mao, was sent back to prison for sentencing.

Young Girl Jumps Out of a Fire Pit 212

Where is Wang Jinfeng Going?

Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, a young girl was lost in the Ping'an Bridge (平安橋) area of Nanshi. The police officer Yao Shaoqiu from the First Section of the First District found her and brought her back to the station. When questioned by the director of the station, she claimed to be Wang Jinfeng, 15 years old, from Wuxi. She used to live in her hometown. In 1920, a doctor she knew in her village coaxed her in every possible way, saying that he would take her to Shanghai for a trip and give her fashionable clothes and delicious food to wear and eat. I was afraid that my parents would notice and scold me, so I did not allow it. Unexpectedly, he forced me to be brought to Shanghai and sold to a prostitute Wang Maotou, a playboy, near the Great World (大世界) to be a prostitute in a brothel. The doctor took all two hundred yuan of the money for me at that time. After I entered the brothel, every day until evening, the madam would take me to the street and force me to receive guests. If there were no customers until midnight, I would be beaten by the madam, so that my body was covered with scars. I thought that I was still young, and it would be difficult to live like this for a long time. So, after lunch today, I took the opportunity to escape. However, because I had nowhere to stay, I was wandering in the streets. He ordered a written report to be sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to arrange for her accommodation.

Mei Yuan Restaurant Summer Hygiene 213

The Mei Yuan Restaurant (梅園酒家) on Simalu (四馬路), founded by Shanghai merchants Yuan Ludeng and Mao Heyuan, is now paying special attention to food hygiene as the summer season approaches, which is of utmost importance. The restaurant pays special attention to this. Cold storage items are all machine-iced, and all utensils are disinfected and cleaned daily. The kitchen equipment is entirely Western-style, and the waiters are dressed in clean white uniforms, providing attentive service. Recently, the weather has gradually become hotter, and the air in the downstairs hall of the restaurant is sufficient. Lunch guests are very enthusiastic. The gift certificates issued by the restaurant are beautifully printed and suitable for weddings and celebrations.

Supplementary Local Edition of Shen Bao

Commentary

Aircraft Bombs Bomb Bengbu City 216

— Fu

Yesterday, according to a telegram from Bengbu, the No. 102 Douglas aircraft of the First Team stationed in Bengbu flew to Guangshan on the morning of the 3rd to bomb the communist bandits. It returned to Bengbu around 9:00 AM. One 35-pound bomb remaining on the plane came loose and fell on the bustling Taiping Street (太平街), killing 22 citizens and injuring 41. All sectors are furious. The recklessness of the pilot should be punished appropriately for harming the citizens.

Judging from the number of the No. 102 aircraft of the First Team stationed in Bengbu, our country has quite a few aircraft. Why was there not a single aircraft participating in the war against the enemy during the Shanghai War? The airfield was built on a large scale. The people's losses are unknown, taking Songjiang as an example, no less than six or seven hundred acres of land were seized. As a result, there was not a shadow of an aircraft. Who is this "Huarong Road" (華容道) set up for? Is it to "scare Sima Yi with the dead Zhuge Liang" (死諸葛嚇生仲達)? What is even more strange is that the war is over now, and it is time for farming, but the airfield is still unwilling to return the land. What is the intention of the authorities?

Originally, our country lacked aircraft pilots and could not fight against Japan on equal footing. I think this kind of aircraft can either be used to eliminate some communist parties, or it can be improved. Now, the citizens of Bengbu have suffered such a major tragedy for no reason. The aircraft pilot is not only technically immature, but also careless and negligent in his duties. His ability and tricks to suppress the communists can be imagined.

No matter what kind of weapon China has, it will not kill the enemy, but only kill its own people. This can be seen from this incident.

The returning horses have ceased fighting at Mount Hua, when will you return my old mountains and rivers? The remnants of the fortress will soon be spring, the sea is calm and the water is not turbulent. Able to express loyalty and anger to be recorded in history, still the green waves wrinkle on Wusong. Few people know the horse of the reverse journey, Yu Xin laments the times and feels much. The poem of the owl destroying the house can be written, what can be done about the haggard people's livelihood?

Science

Aluminum 218

— Jin Huayuan

Among the light metallic elements, there is an element that is very light in weight, which is called Aluminum. In the periodic table, the atomic number is thirteen, and the atomic weight is twenty-seven point two.

Aluminum is not only a very light element in the earth's crust, but also a very abundant element, accounting for about eight percent (8%) of all elements in the earth's crust.

Aluminum was invented by Charles Martin Hall, a student at Oberlin College (奥伯林大學) in Ohio, USA, on February 23, 1886.

In 1827, fifty-nine years before Hall's invention, a famous German chemist, Professor Friedrich Wohler, had experimented with a few small particles of aluminum smaller than dust. Because it was not easy to obtain and the price was high, it did not attract attention. It was not until Hall used his own invented electroanalysis method to extract aluminum in large quantities relatively easily from the ore seed aluminum oxide (ALO).

Aluminum is the same as gold, it is not easy to oxidize in the air, which is the opposite of iron. Its chemical affinity is far less than iron, because iron is very easy to oxidize to form iron oxide, that is, the so-called rust. However, aluminum and gold are also slightly different, that is, gold is absolutely not easy to oxidize, and aluminum sometimes has the possibility of oxidation. However, even after oxidation, it is as difficult to break it down and reduce it to the original substance before oxidation as it is to oxidize it. This is similar to the temperament of some people in our human race. If you want me to do something that I don't want to do, I will never do it. But even if I do it because of some problem, I can't give it up. It's a very strong attitude. Now we see in the market a kind of thermos bottle lid and a kind of small pot, which are very light and not very bright, and the sound of knocking on it is not sharp. This is made of aluminum. In addition, some parts of electrical appliances, teacups, etc. are also made of aluminum, which is light and sensitive, not clumsy. How progressive is this?

End of Article

Shanghai Life 219

— Yi Ping

(3) The Misfortune of White Sugar Plums

"Anyone want to buy white copper (sugar) plums? Twenty cents for one:::"

Along the gap in East Xinqiao Street, A Gen had set up a stall selling sugar plums according to the season. He sat on a high stool, wearing a casual hat tilted to one side, a short shirt and trousers of coarse blue cloth, his upper garment open, revealing the undershirt inside, a silk trousers belt hanging between his legs, in his hand holding a fly whisk, very leisurely lightly brushing a pile of white sugar plums.

"A Gen!" A person similarly dressed, but with a foldable melon-skin hat on his head, ran out from XX Lane opposite, shouting directly at A Gen. A Gen seemed startled, and said with a smile,

"Boss (pronounced Du), long time no see." From the belt pocket of his blue cloth shirt, he took out a box of Golden Mouse brand cigarettes, offering one to the so-called "Boss," and placing one at the corner of his own lips.

The boss lit the cigarette, picked a large white sugar plum from the stall, and stuffed it into his mouth to chew.

"Business is good!" Although the voice was vague, the clever A Gen knew that the visitor had malicious intent.

"Boss, what's the matter?" A Gen said, still wearing a smile.

"A Gen! Stop pretending, you closed down Yanziwo, what about our principal?"

"Boss, don't be angry," A Gen took out two silver dollars from the pocket where he kept the Golden Mouse cigarettes, "Business isn't good today, there are still so many plums."

I couldn’t find you for three days, you are selling sugar plums? A Gen! Pay up, cough up another ten silver dollars, or this grandson will make trouble.

"Boss, we are all family, how about you have a cigarette?" A Gen's words were obviously hardening.

"Fuck you!" He raised his right hand and slapped A Gen in the face.

A Gen, unprepared for this move, also stood up and punched the boss squarely in the chest. Thus, two sets of blue cloth shorts and trousers twisted into a ball, as if one happened to pass by this place, one could hear a string of "fuck your mother" sounds.

Finally, A Gen and the boss were pulled apart by colleagues, their hands held behind their backs, still desperately wanting to move forward. A Gen's casual hat was even more askew, the boss's melon-skin hat had already disappeared. "Fuck you, there will be a day when I finish you off," the boss, pulled away by the crowd with much difficulty, turned around and said, "I'll settle this, fuck you."

A pile of white sugar plums, quietly lying in the muddy ditch beside the sidewalk, sacrificed by the war.

Family Issues

Remarriage of Widowers and Widows 220

— Qiu Yi

Mr. Wang, the owner of the tobacco and paper shop next door, who was already old, his old wife, unfortunately, died of illness last year. Mr. Wang was naturally very sad, and shed a few old tears. Afterwards, we heard Mr. Wang say this to people, "I will never remarry, I am an old man about to be made into a coffin."

Yesterday, the front of the tobacco and paper shop was bustling. Two red candles were lit high in the shop. Many of Mr. Wang's relatives and friends also arrived. Driven by curiosity, I went to inquire with his apprentice, Little Shaoxing.

"Don't you know? Today, the master is marrying a wife!" Little Shaoxing replied with a smile. Mr. Wang's eldest daughter-in-law is a young widow, her husband having died of lung disease three years ago. In addition to buying vegetables, cooking, and managing household affairs, recently, since her mother-in-law passed away, she also had to serve her several younger brothers-in-law. In our view, she is not only a very capable woman, but also a very amiable young woman. It's a pity that she unfortunately entered the Wang family's door, and in less than half a year, she became a widow. Her lifelong happiness was thus buried. In addition to toiling like an ox or a horse all day long, she had virtually no fantasies. Speaking of the word "remarriage", not only had she not thought of it, but even if she did think of it, she would consider it to be against women's virtue and be scolded by others. Moreover, within the Wang family, which was within the sphere of influence of this man-eating ethical code, it was even more absolutely impossible.

Alas! Men who are over half a century old can remarry, can openly and legitimately remarry, while widows who are in their youth cannot remarry, and society and family strictly prevent them from remarrying. In fact, what is the difference between remarriage of widowers and remarriage of widows? This is a morbid state of Chinese society, and a major issue that those engaged in women's movements and those reforming the family system should pay attention to.

There are plenty of people in society who take one mistress after another, and the ridiculous act of arranging marriage with a spirit tablet for unmarried women whose fiancés have unfortunately died, such extremely opposite facts exist in the world.

Shen Ruiqing is found not guilty. ▲Mao Jinbao is sentenced to eight months of imprisonment for recidivist fraud. ▲Zhang Fusheng is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for recidivist night-time theft in a dwelling. ▲Wang Zhiwei is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for theft in a gang of three or more people. ▲Zhu Yusheng is sentenced to one month of imprisonment and fined forty yuan for opium smoking. ▲Yao Luo, Wei Guoan, and Xue Yongxiang are found not guilty. ▲Wu Shoumin is sentenced to twelve years of imprisonment for armed robbery in a gang and Zhou Zhicheng is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for joint intent to supply others with military firearms and ammunition for criminal purposes. (Above, May 30)

Shanghai Second Special District Local Court 223

Civil Judgments

Liu Cheng-lin vs. Wang Qi-rong Rent Arrears Case: The defendant shall pay the plaintiff rent of one thousand one hundred and sixty taels of silver and street sweeping fees of eight taels of silver. The plaintiff's remaining claims are dismissed. Court costs shall be borne by the defendant two-thirds and the plaintiff one-third.

Han Zhi-sun vs. Li Bokao Rent Arrears Case: The defendant shall pay the plaintiff rent of two hundred and eighty taels of silver and return the leased house to the plaintiff. Court costs shall be borne by the defendant. This judgment regarding the return of the leased house is granted provisional execution.

Cao Jin-sheng vs. Zhao Chun-lin Debt Case: The plaintiff's lawsuit is dismissed. Court costs shall be borne by the plaintiff.

Xu Shun-xing Leather Goods Store vs. Shun-xing-xiang Goods Debt Case: The plaintiff's lawsuit is dismissed. Court costs shall be borne by the plaintiff.

Liu Cheng-lin vs. Tianhua Hosiery Factory, Jin Xian-qing, et al. Rent Arrears Case: The defendant Tianhua Hosiery Factory shall pay the plaintiff rent of 625 yuan in foreign currency; Yao Yong-ji shall pay the plaintiff rent of 735 yuan in foreign currency; Huasheng Industrial Society shall pay the plaintiff rent of 840 yuan in foreign currency; and Zhenxin Company shall pay the plaintiff rent of 500 yuan in foreign currency. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendants proportionally.

Yong'an Real Estate Company vs. Yang Zheng-yong Rent Arrears Eviction Case: The defendant shall immediately vacate the premises and pay the plaintiff rent arrears of 924 yuan in foreign currency. The plaintiff's request for provisional execution is rejected. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant.

Zhou Sheng-fa vs. Gu Xin-qiao Land Return Case: The plaintiff's lawsuit is dismissed. Court costs shall be borne by the plaintiff.

Zhou Zhi-ting vs. Li De-qing Rent Arrears Appeal Case: The appeal is dismissed. The second-instance litigation costs shall be borne by the appellant.

Da Li vs. Hengchang Hao Wang Geng-shu Rent Arrears Case: The defendant shall pay the plaintiff rent of 146 yuan and 50 cents in foreign currency and return the leased house to the plaintiff. Court costs shall be borne by the defendant. The first item of this judgment regarding the return of the leased house is granted provisional execution. Regarding the rent arrears, if the plaintiff provides a security deposit of 70 yuan, provisional execution shall be granted.

Xu Zhong-xin vs. Sun De-sheng Goods Debt Appeal Case: The appeal is dismissed. The second-instance litigation costs shall be borne by the appellant.

Yingrui Condensed Milk Company vs. Pao Te-pai-ke Goods Debt Case: The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 85 taels of silver. Court costs shall be borne by the defendant.

Wang Rong-yao vs. Gu'er Bai-ke-xin Debt Appeal Case: The appeal and the appellee's request for provisional execution are both rejected. The second-instance litigation costs shall be borne by the appellant.

Zhou He-shu vs. Shi Bao-quan Goods Debt Case: The appeal is dismissed. The second-instance litigation costs shall be borne by the appellant.

Yongda Zhuang vs. Tongxing Hao, et al. Debt Case: The defendant Tongxing Hao shall repay the plaintiff 160 taels, zero liang, five qian, and three fen of silver; Yongfeng Tai shall repay the plaintiff 60 taels, zero liang, two qian, and three fen of silver; and Chen Hui-ji shall repay the plaintiff 343 taels, seven qian, and seven fen of silver. Litigation costs shall be borne by the defendants proportionally.

Civil Instructions

A Statement of Sovereignty by Vladimir Bababek: This court is executing the case of An Wanglie vs. Bao Wangpaike concerning debt arrears (Initial Character No. 273). An Wanglie applied for and was granted the seizure of the movable property inside No. 78, Notre Dame Road, owned by Bao Wangpaike, to secure the debt. Subsequently, the applicant requested a stay of execution because the case had been settled out of court. Now, the applicant claims that the furniture belongs to the applicant and requests that it be exempted from seizure. If this is true, the applicant should file a separate lawsuit to confirm ownership. However, since the creditor has applied to close the case, there is no need for further seizure. Except for the issue of ownership to be resolved in a separate case, the request for exemption from seizure shall be approved.

Lu Xi-hou's Application to Move the Seized Car for Safekeeping: This case has been scheduled for a hearing on June 4th, and the owner of Yad Automobile has been summoned to court for questioning. The request shall be reviewed and decided after questioning (3rd).
